        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff. (10-13-10-15 cm2 s-1) in the HCNP obtained at 1150 °C is two orders of magnitude lower than that of Li+ in graphite (10-10-10-13 cm2 s-1), indicating that reducing the carbon particle size is very important for improving electrochem. performance.  These measurements also enable a clear visualization of the stepwise reaction phases and rate changes which occur throughout the insertion/extn. processes in HCNP, The electrochem. measurements also show that the nano-sized HCNP obtained at 1150 °C exhibited higher practical capacity at voltages lower than 1.2 V (vs. Na/Na+), as well as a prolonged cycling stability, which is attributed to an optimum spacing of 0.366 nm between the graphitic layers and the nano particular size resulting in a low-barrier Na+ cation insertion.  These results suggest that HCNP is a very promising high-capacity/stability anode for low cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0215ZE-6YJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li3rx9qn55mIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVaqtrrE&amp;md5=93cb764059ea5aaa3841222611c03416</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.08.119"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, B.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lignin-based electrospun carbon nanofibrous webs as free-standing and binder-free electrodes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Juan; Yu, Bao-jun; Shi, Zhi-qiang; Wang, Cheng-yang; Chong, Chuan-bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">272</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">800-807</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost and bio-based carbon nanofibrous webs (PL-CNFs) are fabricated from polyacrylonitrile (PAN)-refined lignin (RL) which is extd. from hardwood lignosulfonate via simple eletrospinning followed by stabilization and carbonization.  The effects of the PAN/RL mass ratios varying from 9/1,7/3 to 5/5 and heat-treatment temps. (HTTs) in the range from 800, 1000 to 1300 °C on morphol. and structure of PL-CNFs are systematically studied.  Due to unique morphol. and weakly ordered turbostratic microstructure of the 3-D conductive composite networks, the PL-CNFs anode obtained at 1300 °C with a mass ratio of 5/5 exhibits a high reversible capacity of 292.6 mA h g-1 with an initial efficiency of 70.5% at a const. c.d. of 0.02 A g-1 when used as free-standing and binder-free anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  The anode also presents high rate capability (210 and 80 mA h g-1 at 0.4 and 1 A g-1, resp.) and excellent cycle stability (247 mA h g-1 reversible capacity with 90.2% capacity retention ratio at 0.1 A g-1 over 200 cycles).  It is demonstrated that biomass waste lignin can be applied as a promising precursor to fabricate low-cost-high performance carbon electrode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6xoSPzjjd3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgAmbxG1-D2jQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFCnsr3F&amp;md5=f017b8fdfb8a99b1a0c2b4e860724993</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/nl3016957"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Insertion in Hollow Carbon Nanowires for Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yuliang; Xiao, Lifen; Sushko, Maria L.; Wang, Wei; Schwenzer, Birgit; Xiao, Jie; Nie, Zimin; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhengguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C). The good Na-ion insertion property is attributed to the short diffusion distance in the hollow carbon nanowires and the large interlayer distance (0.37 nm) between the graphitic sheets, which agrees with the interlayered distance predicted by theor. calcns. to enable Na-ion insertion in carbon materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9utH1EdajJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgAmbxG1-D2jQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XotlShu78%253D&amp;md5=c54fcb809a340c023d9185f1d9f5e848</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/nl401952h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although different kinds of metal oxide nanoparticles continue to be proposed as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries, their cycle life and power d. are still not suitable for com. applications.  Metal oxide nanoparticles have a large storage capacity, but they suffer from the excessive generation of solid-electrolyte interphase on the surface, low elec. cond., and mech. degrdn. and pulverization resulted from severe vol. expansion during cycling.  Herein we present the prepn. of mesoporous iron oxide nanoparticle clusters by a bottom-up self-assembly approach and demonstrate that they exhibit excellent cyclic stability and rate capability derived from their three-dimensional mesoporous nanostructure.  By controlling the geometric configuration, we can achieve stable interfaces between the electrolyte and active materials, resulting in solid-electrolyte interphase formation confined on the outer surface of the mesoporous iron oxide nanoparticle clusters.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-15JkZmTfF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgAmbxG1-D2jQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtF2rurbO&amp;md5=1d05719c6dd41817fa6b84f5bc7aa0ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-016-0981-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, K.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xue; Zhang, Kai; Lei, Kaixiang; Li, Fujun; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and electrochem. sodium storage of cobalt disulfide (CoS2) with various micro/nano-structures.  CoS2 with microscale sizes are either assembled by nanoparticles (P-CoS2) via a facile solvothermal route or nanooctahedrons constructed solid (O-CoS2) and hollow microstructures (H-CoS2) fabricated by hydrothermal methods.  Among three morphologies, H-CoS2 exhibits the largest discharge capacities and best rate performance as anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Furthermore, H-CoS2 delivers a capacity of 690 mA·h·g-1 at 1 A·g-1 after 100 cycles in a potential range of 0.1-3.0 V, and ∼240 mA·h·g-1 over 800 cycles in the potential window of 1.0-3.0 V.  This cycling difference mainly lies in the two discharge plateaus obsd. in 0.1-3.0 V and one discharge plateau in 1.0-3.0 V.  To interpret the reactions, X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) are applied.  The results show that at the first plateau around 1.4 V, the insertion reaction (CoS2 + xNa+ + xe- → NaxCoS2) occurs; while at the second plateau around 0.6 V, the conversion reaction (NaxCoS2 + (4 - x) Na+ + (4 - x)e- → Co + 2Na2S) takes place.  This provides insights for electrochem. sodium storage of CoS2 as the anode of SIBs.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Inexpensive Antimony Nanocrystals and Their Composites with Red Phosphorus as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Walter, Marc; Erni, Rolf; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries increasingly become of immense research interest as a potential inexpensive alternative to Lithium-ion batteries.  Development of high-energy-d. neg. electrodes (anodes) remains to be a great challenge, esp. because of significant differences between lithium and sodium chemistries.  Two Na-ion anode materials - antimony (Sb) and phosphorus (P) - have been recently shown to offer excellent cycling stability (Sb) and highest known Na-ion charge storage capacity (P).  In this work we report on the synergistic Na-ion storage in a P/Sb/Cu-nanocomposite, produced by mixing inexpensive colloidal Sb nanocrystals with red P and with copper (Cu) nanowires.  In comparison to electrodes composed of only phosphorus, such P/Sb/Cu-composite shows much greater cycling stability providing a capacity of above 1100 mAh g-1 after 50 charge/discharge cycles at a c.d. of 125 mA g-1.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2922</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2eaW1_F18Bfx5Lntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b05653"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing Sodium Ion Battery Performance by Strongly Binding Nanostructured Sb2S3 on Sulfur-Doped Graphene Sheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xunhui; Wang, Guanhua; Lin, Yuwei; Wang, Ying; Ou, Xing; Zheng, Fenghua; Yang, Chenghao; Wang, Jeng-Han; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10953-10959</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising alternative to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.  However, their inferior electrochem. performances, esp. cyclability, become the major challenge for further development of SIBs.  Large vol. change and sluggish diffusion kinetics are generally considered to be responsible for the fast capacity degrdn.  We report the strong chem. bonding of nanostructured Sb2S3 on S-doped graphene sheets (Sb2S3/SGS) that enables a stable capacity retention of 83% for 900 cycles with high capacities and excellent rate performances.  To the best of our knowledge, the cycling performance of the Sb2S3/SGS composite is superior to those reported for any other Sb-based materials for SIBs.  Computational calcns. demonstrate that S-doped graphene (SGS) has a stronger affinity for Sb2S3 and the discharge products than pure graphene, resulting in a robust composite architecture for outstanding cycling stability.  Our study shows a feasible and effective way to solve the long-term cycling stability issue for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCGE30ZIPm4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lih8mSfU5jYDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVGnsbnM&amp;md5=bf18bc0bdfb7f9241bfba0fe990d1c93</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402833"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-Layered SnS2 on Few-Layered Reduced Graphene Oxide as Na-Ion Battery Anode with Ultralong Cycle Life and Superior Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yandong; Zhu, Peiyi; Huang, Liliang; Xie, Jian; Zhang, Shichao; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.  The SnS2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, ultralong cycle life, and superior rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 649 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g.  At 800 mA/g (1.8C), it can yield an initial charge capacity of 469 mA-h/g, which can be maintained at 89% and 61%, resp., after 400 and 1000 cycles.  The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.  The fast and stable Na-storage ability of SnS2/rGO makes it a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2sS3KKxaUkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lih8mSfU5jYDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ms7jI&amp;md5=173a3c027a58922c59d5633c7a05d580</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201701827"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NASICON-Structured NaSn2(PO4)3 with Excellent High-Rate Properties as Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Pu; Ma, Jun; Wang, Tianshi; Qin, Bingsheng; Zhang, Chuanjian; Shang, Chaoqun; Zhao, Jianghui; Cui, Guanglei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6668-6674</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Advanced Li-ion batteries with high rate properties are in high demand and have generated much attention in the research community.  Here, we present a simple sol-gel and solid-state reaction to synthesize NASICON-structured NaSn2(PO4)3 as anode material for lithium-ion batteries.  The obtained material exhibits excellent cycling performance and high rate capacity for half cell and LiFePO4/NaSn2(PO4)3 full cell.  Cyclic voltammograms (CV) and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) were used to analyze the kinetics and thermodn. of the electrode.  Morphol. and structure evolution of the NaSn2(PO4)3 electrode after cycling were explored by transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  These results showed nanoscale Sn was uniformly dispersed in the lithium phosphate matrix during the first discharge.  It is proposed that the enhanced properties are attributed to the "in situ" formation of the ionic conductor as protective matrixes, which prevents the aggregation of nanoparticles during the cycling and provides Li+ diffusion channels in the electrode for fast electrochem. reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrs6URaQqapg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUppsxrcFrZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhs7vN&amp;md5=04ac0a6342cbdc3a11be309d233fe998</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/S0013-4686(02)00017-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Behm, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Irvine, J.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUppsxrcFrZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Q.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb nanoparticles encapsulated into porous carbon matrixes for high-performance lithium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Zheng; Han, Qigang; Zan, Ping; Wu, Yaoming; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel Sb/C polyhedra composite is successfully fabricated by a galvanic replacement reaction technique using metal org. frameworks as templates.  In this composite, the ultrasmall Sb nanoparticles with an av. size of 15 nm are homogeneously encapsulated into the carbon matrixes, forming a hierarchical porous structure with nanosized building blocks.  Used as an anode material for lithium ion batteries, this composite exhibits high lithium storage capacities, excellent rate capability and superior cycle stability, higher than many reported results.  Notably, a discharge capacity of 565 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 is delivered after 100 repeated cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1, a discharge capacity of 400.5 mAh g-1 is also maintained after 500 cycles.  Such superior cycling stability and rate discharge performance of the designed Sb/C composite can be attributed to the synergistic effect between Sb nanoparticles and the porous carbon matrixes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHw3UxCNWEx7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUppsxrcFrZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFSns7zI&amp;md5=5e1981e947065a0326ac81dead49d40a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201700522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, F.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Size and Composition Effects in Sb-Carbon Nanocomposites for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramireddy, Thrinathreddy; Sharma, Neeraj; Xing, Tan; Chen, Ying; Leforestier, Jeremie; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">30152-30164</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are in the spotlight as viable alternatives to lithium-ion batteries in stationary storage and power grid applications.  Among possible anode materials, Sb is one of the interesting candidates due to a combination of battery-type potential plateaus in the charge-discharge profiles, high capacity (theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1), and demonstrated good cyclic stability.  The effect of Sb particle size (particularly at the nanoscale range) and the compn. of Sb-carbon composites on the electrode performance, stability, and charge storage mechanism is systematically evaluated here for the first time.  A range of Sb-carbon nanocomposites with varied Sb particle size (between 50 and ∼1 nm) are studied.  The control of the particle size is achieved via varying the carbon and Sb wt. ratio in the precursors.  The shape of charge-discharge profiles, hysteresis, and the difference in cyclic stabilities and rate performance are analyzed.  The nanocomposite with the smallest particle size (∼1 nm) and the largest carbon content provides the most stable cyclic behavior and a better rate capability but suffers from an increased hysteresis between charge and discharge curves.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction expts. indicate that the storage mechanism in the Sb-carbon nanocomposites contg. Sb nanoparticles is different from the electrodes with bulkier, micron-sized Sb particles, and the electrochem. reaction proceeds through a no. of cryst. intermediates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZu3AXRGlszLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljS2ZGxPOun6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslSisbbF&amp;md5=dee25eed73684b841e7a3cbdfa71accc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b13193"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Dimensional Yolk-Shell Sb@Ti-O-P Nanostructures as a High-Capacity and High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-Dimensional Yolk-Shell Sb@Ti-O-P Nanostructures as a High-Capacity and High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Bai, Zhongchao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">447-454</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of high energy/power d. and long cycle life of anode materials is highly desirable for sodium ion batteries, because graphite anode cannot be used directly.  Sb stands out from the potential candidates, due to high capacity, good electronic cond., and moderate sodiation voltage.  Here, one-dimensional yolk-shell Sb@Ti-O-P nanostructures are synthesized by reducing core-shell Sb2O3@TiO2 nanorods with NaH2PO2.  This structure has Sb nanorod as the core to increase the capacity and Ti-O-P as the shell to stabilize the interface between electrolyte and electrode material.  The gap between the core and the shell accommodates the vol. change during sodiation/desodiation.  These features endow the structure outstanding performances.  It could deliver a capacity of about 760 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at 500 mA g-1, with a capacity retention of about 94%.  Even at 10 A g-1, the reversible capacity is still at 360 mA h g-1.  The full battery of Sb@Ti-O-P//Na3V2(PO4)3-C presents a high output voltage (∼2.7 V) and a capacity of 392 mA h g-1anode after 150 cycles at 1 A g-1anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwmtxRb5CFALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljS2ZGxPOun6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2ksrjJ&amp;md5=2a9bcad7fdd487ab4d2b2d9e71fec387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Q.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous Phosphorus/Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Paper for Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Chao; Wang, Xi; Liang, Qifeng; Liu, Xizheng; Weng, Qunhong; Liu, Jiangwei; Yang, Yijun; Dai, Zhonghua; Ding, Kejian; Bando, Yoshio; Tang, Jie; Golberg, Dmitri</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic structure and migration dynamics of MoS2/LixMoS2 interface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Shulin; Wang, Liping; Shao, Ruiwen; Zou, Jian; Cai, Ran; Lin, Jinhuang; Zhu, Chongyang; Zhang, Jingmin; Xu, Feng; Cao, Jian; Feng, Jicai; Qi, Junlei; Gao, Peng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">560-568</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The performance of alkali-metal-ion batteries largely depends on the migration behavior of alkali metal ions in the electrodes.  Probing the at. structure of the reaction interface and the dynamic process during ion transport in the electrodes will help better understand the underlying electrochem. mechanisms and inspire rational electrode designs.  In this study, by combining in situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and aberration-cor. scanning TEM (STEM), we track the reversible lithium ion transport in MoS2 nanostructures to reveal the at. structure and dynamic behaviors of the reaction interface.  We find that lithium ions insertion triggers complex phase transformations.  Three different phases co-exist at the interface: a pristine 2H phase, a 1T phase with a shrank lattice const. of -3.3% (±2.3%), and a distorted 1T phase (called 1T' phase) with an expanded lattice const. of 5.5% (±2.5%).  The atomically resolved Z-contrast image shows that the expanded 1T' phase has distorted Mo arrangements.  Furthermore, the lithium ions migration causes defects at the reaction front, and the diffusion on the surface is faster than that inside, forming a core-shell structure at the reaction interface.  The diffusivity of lithium ions is directly measured to be ∼1000-30,000 nm2/s, which is significantly higher than that of sodium insertion (∼10-20 nm2/s).  The at.-scale observations of lithium-ion-migration-induced complex structural evolutions would help understand the properties of MoS2 nanostructures and shed light on the design of alkali-metal-ion batteries with general transition-metal dichalcogenide electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3AuZNQ1MlHbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQY29Rq82tAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXns1Sqs7Y%253D&amp;md5=7a40e49d0ce3697a5186991506d5f455</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b04950"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic-Scale Probing of the Dynamics of Sodium Transport and Intercalation-Induced Phase Transformations in MoS<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">11296</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11301</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.5b04950</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D11296-11301%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DP.%2BGao%26author%3DL.%2BP.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BY.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26author%3DK.%2BH.%2BLiu%26title%3DAtomic-Scale%2BProbing%2Bof%2Bthe%2BDynamics%2Bof%2BSodium%2BTransport%2Band%2BIntercalation-Induced%2BPhase%2BTransformations%2Bin%2BMoS2%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.5b04950&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b08065&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.5b04950&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic-Scale Probing of the Dynamics of Sodium Transport and Intercalation-Induced Phase Transformations in MoS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Peng; Wang, Liping; Zhang, Yuyang; Huang, Yuan; Liu, Kaihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11296-11301</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For alkali-metal-ion batteries, probing the dynamic processes of ion transport in electrodes is crit. to gain insights into understanding how the electrode functions and thus how the authors can improve it.  Here, by using in situ high-resoln. TEM, the authors probe the dynamics of Na transport in MoS2 nanostructures in real-time and compare the intercalation kinetics with previous lithium insertion.  Na intercalation follows the two-phase reaction mechanism, i.e., trigonal prismatic 2H-MoS2 → octahedral 1T-NaMoS2, and the phase boundary is ∼2 nm thick.  The velocity of the phase boundary at &lt;10 nm/s is 1 order smaller than that of lithium diffusion, suggesting sluggish kinetics for sodium intercalation.  The newly formed 1T-NaMoS2 contains a high d. of defects and series superstructure domains with typical sizes of ∼3-5 nm.  The authors' results provide valuable insights into finding suitable Na electrode materials and understanding the properties of transition metal dichalcogenide MoS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2AijIdeeGI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQY29Rq82tAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFejtrjO&amp;md5=0f587a13908ef0ed2eb9e73a5dc858b6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201606860"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soto, F. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, P. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Engelhard, M. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marzouk, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoconfined antimony in sulfur and nitrogen co-doped three-dimensionally (3D) interconnected macroporous carbon for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Chenglong; Li, Weihan; Yang, Zhenzhong; Gu, Lin; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12-19</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Sb encapsulated in S and N co-doped three-dimensionally (3D) interconnected macroporous carbon composite (denoted as Sb@S,N-3DPC) has been fabricated by using silica opals as hard template following a carbonization process.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform 3D-network structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon spherical shell.  The Sb@S,N-3DPC electrode shows a high reversible capacity of 482 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, displaying good capacity stability (∼93% of the initial discharge capacity after 500 cycles at 100 mA g-1).  The electrode displays superior rate capability and ultralong cyclability (255 mAh g-1 at 2 Ag-1after 2000 cycles) and also reveals a good rate capability that maintains 160 mAh g-1 at 5 Ag-1.  The excellent electrochem. performance of the Sb@S,N-3DPC is attributed to the 3D-porous carbon network structure and uniform distribution of Sb nanoparticles in carbon matrix, enhancing the cond., holding the structure integrity, and thus improving the cycling performance of the anode material.  In addn., sulfur and nitrogen co-doping introduced more defects and active sites to the carbon framework, thereby improving the interfacial adsorption and electrochem. behaviors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqX7jYTHbqsH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQY29Rq82tAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Sqs7jO&amp;md5=5bb2cf2da6c2a3e6f8ae299d49db60c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>134</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20805</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">20811</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixVzXaQ9G96g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/nl404165c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kravchyk, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Walter, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kovalenko, M.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monodisperse Antimony Nanocrystals for High-Rate Li-ion and Na-ion Battery Anodes: Nano versus Bulk</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Meng; Kravchyk, Kostiantyn; Walter, Marc; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1255-1262</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).  At all C-rates (0.5-20C, e.g. current densities of 0.33-13.2 A/g), capacities of 20 nm Sb particles are systematically better than for both 10 nm and bulk Sb.  At 20C rate, retention of charge storage capacities by 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals can reach 78-85% of the low-rate value, indicating that rate capability of Sb nanostructures can be comparable to the best Li-ion intercalation anodes and is so far unprecedented for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5xNSHYkxGf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixVzXaQ9G96g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1Wmsbw%253D&amp;md5=6c9a0c090f52077a9b8eda7847cbfe2f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201304962"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, L.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlling SEI Formation on SnSb-Porous Carbon Nanofibers for Improved Na Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ji, Liwen; Gu, Meng; Shao, Yuyan; Li, Xiaolin; Engelhard, Mark H.; Arey, Bruce W.; Wang, Wei; Nie, Zimin; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Chongmin; Zhang, Ji-Guang; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metallurgically lithiated SiOx anode with high capacity and ambient air compatibility</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Sun, Jie; Yan, Kai; Liu, Yayuan; Liu, Wei; Lu, Zhenda; Lin, Dingchang; Zhou, Guangmin; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">113</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A common issue plaguing battery anodes is the large consumption of lithium in the initial cycle as a result of the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase followed by gradual loss in subsequent cycles.  It presents a need for prelithiation to compensate for the loss.  However, anode prelithiation faces the challenge of high chem. reactivity because of the low anode potential.  Previous efforts have produced prelithiated Si nanoparticles with dry air stability, which cannot be stabilized under ambient air.  Here, we developed a one-pot metallurgical process to synthesize LixSi/Li2O composites by using low-cost SiO or SiO2 as the starting material.  The resulting composites consist of homogeneously dispersed LixSi nanodomains embedded in a highly cryst. Li2O matrix, providing the composite excellent stability even in ambient air with 40% relative humidity.  The composites are readily mixed with various anode materials to achieve high first cycle Coulombic efficiency (CE) of &gt;100% or serve as an excellent anode material by itself with stable cyclability and consistently high CEs (99.81% at the seventh cycle and ∼99.87% for subsequent cycles).  Therefore, LixSi/Li2O composites achieved balanced reactivity and stability, promising a significant boost to lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1AoXhyyaR-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixVzXaQ9G96g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpvFekt7g%253D&amp;md5=40b8bc19b7b13b1f9459af9777bf4e71</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-017-1501-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simple synthesis of a porous Sb/Sb2O3 nanocomposite for a high-capacity anode material in Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Wang, Nana; Zhou, Yanli; Yang, Xianfeng; Zhou, Wenyao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1794-1803</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-capacity anode materials are highly desirable for sodium ion batteries.  Here, a porous Sb/Sb2O3 nanocomposite is successfully synthesized by the mild oxidization of Sb nanocrystals in air.  In the composite, Sb contributes good cond. and Sb2O3 improves cycling stability, particularly within the voltage window of 0.02-1.5 V.  It remains at a reversible capacity of 540 mAh·g-1 after 180 cycles at 0.66 A·g-1.  Even at 10 A·g-1, the reversible capacity is still preserved at 412 mAh·g-1, equiv. to 71.6% of that at 0.066 A·g-1.  These results are much better than Sb nanocrystals with a similar size and structure.  Expanding the voltage window to 0.02-2.5 V includes the conversion reaction between Sb2O3 and Sb into the discharge/charge profiles.  This would induce a large vol. change and high structure strain/stress, deteriorating the cycling stability.  The identification of a proper voltage window for Sb/Sb2O3 paves the way for its development in sodium ion batteries.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNvZJc1ACQJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/ja8057309"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brezesinski, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Polleux, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tolbert, S. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Templated Nanocrystal-Based Porous TiO<sub>2</sub> Films for Next-Generation Electrochemical Capacitors</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2009</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>131</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1802</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1809</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Templated Nanocrystal-Based Porous TiO2 Films for Next-Generation Electrochemical Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Dunn, Bruce; Tolbert, Sarah H.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">131</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1802-1809</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages in using nanoscale materials for electrochem. energy storage are generally attributed to short diffusion path lengths for both electronic and lithium ion transport.  Here, another contribution, the charge storage from faradaic processes occurring at the surface, referred to as pseudocapacitive effect are considered.  This paper describes the synthesis and pseudocapacitive characteristics of block copolymer templated anatase TiO2 thin films synthesized using either sol-gel reagents or preformed nanocrystals as building blocks.  Both materials are highly cryst. and have large surface areas; however, the structure of the porosity is not identical.  The different titania systems were characterized by a combination of small- and wide-angle x-ray diffraction/scattering, combined with SEM imaging and physisorption measurements.  Following the authors' previously reported approach, the authors are able to use the voltammetric sweep rate dependence to det. quant. the capacitive contribution to the current response.  Considerable enhancement of the electrochem. properties results when the films are both made from nanocrystals and mesoporous.  Such materials show high levels of capacitive charge storage and high insertion capacities.  By contrast, when mesoscale porosity is created in a material with dense walls (rather than porous walls derived from the aggregation of nanocrystals), insertion capacities comparable to templated nanocrystal films can be achieved, but the capacitance is much lower.  The results presented here illustrate the importance of pseudocapacitive behavior that develops in high surface area mesoporous oxide films.  Such systems provide a new class of pseudocapacitive materials, which offer increased charge storage without compromising charge storage kinetics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcoE8HPLZjM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNvZJc1ACQJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXptlOntg%253D%253D&amp;md5=5f84762c9796e440f61947bd2b9d39f5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms12122"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Array of nanosheets render ultrafast and high-capacity Na-ion storage by tunable pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Yang, Peihua; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Wang, Jin; Fan, Xiaofeng; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Fan, Hong Jin; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a potentially low-cost and safe alternative to the prevailing lithium-ion battery technol.  However, it is a great challenge to achieve fast charging and high power d. for most sodium-ion electrodes because of the sluggish sodiation kinetics.  Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.  The graphene foam supported tin(II) sulfide nanoarray anode delivers a high reversible capacity of ∼1,100 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 and ∼420 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1, which even outperforms its lithium-ion storage performance.  The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVSw-KQ43s-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNvZJc1ACQJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFSqtLbO&amp;md5=3f7ab452279e7159794a832183e58387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficiency of ab-initio total energy calculations for metals and semiconductors using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmuller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Computational Materials Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present a detailed description and comparison of algorithms for performing ab-initio quantum-mech. calcns. using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  The authors will discuss: (a) partial occupancies within the framework of the linear tetrahedron method and the finite temp. d.-functional theory, (b) iterative methods for the diagonalization of the Kohn-Sham Hamiltonian and a discussion of an efficient iterative method based on the ideas of Pulay's residual minimization, which is close to an order N2atoms scaling even for relatively large systems, (c) efficient Broyden-like and Pulay-like mixing methods for the charge d. including a new special preconditioning optimized for a plane-wave basis set, (d) conjugate gradient methods for minimizing the electronic free energy with respect to all degrees of freedom simultaneously.  The authors have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VAMP (Vienna ab-initio mol.-dynamics package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semi-conducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLsfJmf_ZpQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhNvZJc1ACQJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28XmtFWgsrk%253D&amp;md5=779b9a71bbd32904f968e39f39946190</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">FurthmÜLler, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes for Ab Initio Total-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11169-11186</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoK9e6g4dZiorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZMrNxS6Q_-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28Xms1Whu7Y%253D&amp;md5=9c8f6f298fe5ffe37c2589d3f970a697</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.92.246401"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dion, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rydberg, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schröder, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langreth, D.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Van der Waals Density Functional for General Geometries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dion, M.; Rydberg, H.; Schroeder, E.; Langreth, D. C.; Lundqvist, B. I.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">92</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">246401/1-246401/4</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A scheme within d. functional theory is proposed that provides a practical way to generalize to unrestricted geometries the method applied with some success to layered geometries [H. Rydberg et al., Phys. Rev. Lett. 91, 126402 (2003)].  It includes van der Waals forces in a seamless fashion.  By expansion to second order in a carefully chosen quantity contained in the long-range part of the correlation functional, the nonlocal correlations are expressed in terms of a d.-d. interaction formula.  It contains a relatively simple parametrized kernel, with parameters detd. by the local d. and its gradient.  The proposed functional is applied to rare gas and benzene dimers, where it is shown to give a realistic description.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNKJSkCZkLk7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZMrNxS6Q_-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2cXltVerur4%253D&amp;md5=abbf50b023000f126ba66af15c786583</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1088/0953-8984/22/2/022201"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Klimeš, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bowler, D.
